<div id="review_1255121507" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1255121507" />
    <a title="Snotchocheez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1899836-snotchocheez"><img alt="Snotchocheez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510561146p2/1899836.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1255121507?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Snotchocheez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Snotchocheez" href="/user/show/1899836-snotchocheez">Snotchocheez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1255121507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14736744204898532496">I probably need to file Joe R. Lansdale in the "Southern Authors I need to keep an eye on" file (if I may be so bold as to lump someone from East Texas into the "South"). I was consistently delighted by my first encounter with his work, the creepy cool 1930's-era Texas Gothic thriller <i>The Bottoms</i>. Much as I found Wiley Cash (another Southern author I've discovered recently) a straightforward, no-nonsense storyteller, Lansdale's style doesn't make room for ornate prose. It's all about establishin</span>
  <span id="freeText14736744204898532496" style="display:none">I probably need to file Joe R. Lansdale in the "Southern Authors I need to keep an eye on" file (if I may be so bold as to lump someone from East Texas into the "South"). I was consistently delighted by my first encounter with his work, the creepy cool 1930's-era Texas Gothic thriller <i>The Bottoms</i>. Much as I found Wiley Cash (another Southern author I've discovered recently) a straightforward, no-nonsense storyteller, Lansdale's style doesn't make room for ornate prose. It's all about establishing setting, creating characters the reader wants to know better, engaging with uncertainties. No flowery gewgaws or cheap devices to be had here: just smart storytelling.<br /><br />I had reported in a status update that this reminded me quite a bit of <i>To Kill a Mockingbird</i>, though it's probably not fair to compare them; there's not too much overlap storywise. Rather, the <i>feelings</i> Lansdale tale left me with were not unlike those that of Harper Lee's beloved fictional (but very real for the day and time) account of racial injustice. Much like Ms. Lee's Jim Crow-era'd Alabama, <i>The Bottoms</i> has as its backdrop the racial divide in Depression Era East Texas. The story is capably recounted in flashback by octogenarian Harry Crane of his life in the Bottoms (a briar-y mucky morass along the Sabine River) of gruesome goings-on back when he and his younger sister Tomasina ('Tom') were kids. One day while exploring the neighboring Bottoms, Harry and Tom encounter a badly decomposed body of a 'colored' woman strung up with baling wire. This news, after reported to their father (constable Jacob Crane), was met with a collective shrug by most of the white populace ('oh, another N----- whore kilt, big deal' was the prevailing attitude). The black folks were naturally more fearful, yet sanguine, throwing around the "Goat Man" or "Travelling Man" (hobo) lore around to attribute the murder to. The kids (and naturally their constable father) just wanted justice for the killed woman. As a few more brutally murdered corpses start turning up around the Sabine, however, they realize that justice is not going be swift or blind. As allegations by Constable Jacob start flying, the Ku Klux Klan (and its supporters) start meting out justice of its own. <br /><br />As murder mysteries go, this one wasn't all that taut (even idjit me had this figured out by about the midway mark) but you'll probably overlook that in favor of the sweaty sordidness of the wretched tableaux Lansdale's painted for the reader. He puts you right there in the thick of it, bushwhacking through the brambles, sweating as the protagonists sift the Bottoms for the truth. I devoured this quickly, but I'm certain it will stay with me for quite a while. He's got many novels and short stories under his belt before and since this 2000 release; I can't wait to explore them all.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14736744204898532496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_101943451" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101943451" />
    <a title="Lou" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3699303-lou"><img alt="Lou" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312212794p2/3699303.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101943451?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lou" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lou" href="/user/show/3699303-lou">Lou</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3699303-lou?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3699303-lou?shelf=march-2012">march-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101943451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5521554800080491896">The main protagonist Harry Crane takes us back to his youth to the time of the 1930's. He tells of his growing up in the family farm in the Bottoms, of their struggles during the great Depression and the grizzly murdered women that they discover in the Bottoms. He tells of his wonders of his youth and his delight in learning of those around him during his coming of age, of his quest and mystery in search of the identity of The Goat Man. <br/><br/>His poor Dog Toby a limp but courageous dog that you'll nev</span>
  <span id="freeText5521554800080491896" style="display:none">The main protagonist Harry Crane takes us back to his youth to the time of the 1930's. He tells of his growing up in the family farm in the Bottoms, of their struggles during the great Depression and the grizzly murdered women that they discover in the Bottoms. He tells of his wonders of his youth and his delight in learning of those around him during his coming of age, of his quest and mystery in search of the identity of The Goat Man. <br /><br />His poor Dog Toby a limp but courageous dog that you'll never forget and his equally brave and lovely sister Tom. That loving kind ma and his grandma really a character to remember his father a stand up righteous kind of guy, a tough law man that wishes to see beyond skin colour. They faces problems with K.K.K members in the search for the murderer. As the story progresses more peoples true colours start to show.<br /><br /> The Bottoms be a place you would love and hate to live, mark my words it sure is a place and a story to remember of as long as you live. It pays homage to the great novel To Kill a Mockingbird, has everything that story stood for and leaves the reader with a similar awe. <br /><br />Well deserved of the Edgar Award. <br /><br />This story is just as good as his new novel <a href="http://more2read.com/review/edge-of-dark-water-by-joe-r-lansdale/" rel="nofollow noopener">Edge of Dark Water</a> also taken place during the depression era with equally wonderful and memorable characters.<br /><br />The story is presented before you in easy flowing storytelling way, a poignant tale of human endeavour against odds, yet another Joe Lansdale great story with wonderful prose. A joy to read full of heart and horrors, a fully immersive reading of a great story.<br /><br />Once completing this story you would be in regret due to no longer being in company with these characters just as the main protagonist mentions in his recollections...<br /><strong> "Each time i visit now, close my eyes to go there, i hope when i awake i will no longer be of this world, but one where Mama and Daddy, Tom and Grandma, perhaps even Mose and the Goat Man, and of course good old Toby, will be waiting for me."</strong><br /><br />Watch out for a movie adaptation that is going to be released, this would be a really good movie especially starring with Bill Paxton as an actor.<br /><br /><strong><br /> <blockquote>"Just a short time before I had been a happy kid with no worries. I didn't even know it was the Depression, let alone there were murderers outside of the magazines I read down at the barbershop, and none f the magazines I read had to do with killers who did this kind of thing. And Daddy, though a good man, sincere and true, if briefly distracted, was no Doc Savage.<br /> In the detective magazines the cops and private eyes saw a clue two, they put it together. Cracked the whole case wide open. In real life, there were clues a plenty, but instead of cracking the case open, they just made it all the more confusing."<br /><br />"Daddy was often chastised by certain church-minded folks for keeping pulps handy at the barbershop. But as my Dad always explained about racy covers, it's just a little paint, folks. Nobody's naked."<br /><br />"Another thing different then was you learned about things like dying when you were quite young. It couldn't be helped. You raised and killed chickens and hogs, hunted and fished, so you were constantly up against it. That being the case, I think we respected life more than some do now, and useless suffering was not to be tolerated." </blockquote><br /></strong><br /><br />Read my interview with the author @ <a href="http://more2read.com/review/interview-with-joe-r-lansdale/" rel="nofollow noopener">http://more2read.com/review/interview-with-joe-r-lansdale/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5521554800080491896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer820356519550336293">Remember, Chilluns, It's Always A Sin To Rip Off A Mocking Bird!<br/><br/>All right, I loved BUBBA HOTEP. The movie, not the book. And I did enjoy a couple of Joe R. Lansdale stories that I read in the collection HIGH COTTON. ("Godzilla's 12 Step Program" was a special favorite.) But when he tries to turn all "lit'rary" and create a poignant coming of age novel . . . well, that hound dog don't hunt. <br/><br/>Everything here is something you've seen before . . . many, many times before. Sensitive boy narrator? Chec</span>
  <span id="freeText820356519550336293" style="display:none">Remember, Chilluns, It's Always A Sin To Rip Off A Mocking Bird!<br /><br />All right, I loved BUBBA HOTEP. The movie, not the book. And I did enjoy a couple of Joe R. Lansdale stories that I read in the collection HIGH COTTON. ("Godzilla's 12 Step Program" was a special favorite.) But when he tries to turn all "lit'rary" and create a poignant coming of age novel . . . well, that hound dog don't hunt. <br /><br />Everything here is something you've seen before . . . many, many times before. Sensitive boy narrator? Check. Strong but flawed father? Check. Peppery old lady with a heart of gold? Check. Darkies who know their place but are ever so grateful when folks give them just a little bit more? Check. <br /><br />Two stars for good nature descriptions and really knowing the rural South. Other than that . . .<br /><br />If H.P. Lovecraft tried to write IT'S A WONDERFUL LIFE, this is what he might have come up with. <br /><br />Shudder!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1528829052" />
    <a title="Camie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7399266-camie"><img alt="Camie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571025937p2/7399266.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1528829052?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Camie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Camie" href="/user/show/7399266-camie">Camie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1528829052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16729440389828374258">From his nursing home bed Harry Collins recalls some of the suspenseful events of coming up in post Depression times in the swampy " bottoms" of East Texas. This coming of age tale about the summer he and his sister Tom stumble upon the mutilated dead corpse of a black woman and get the entire town caught up in a whirlwind of uncertainty and racial conflict, is a winner of The Edgar and American Mystery Awards. The books blurb cites it as a thriller with echoes of William Faulkner and Harper Lee</span>
  <span id="freeText16729440389828374258" style="display:none">From his nursing home bed Harry Collins recalls some of the suspenseful events of coming up in post Depression times in the swampy " bottoms" of East Texas. This coming of age tale about the summer he and his sister Tom stumble upon the mutilated dead corpse of a black woman and get the entire town caught up in a whirlwind of uncertainty and racial conflict, is a winner of The Edgar and American Mystery Awards. The books blurb cites it as a thriller with echoes of William Faulkner and Harper Lee. I did see a few similarities, as the father in the story Constable Jacob Collins is charged with trying to uphold the law at a time when aiding a black person could result in the KKK burning a cross in your yard, and it's told in a no nonsense form which is similar to some Faulkner's tales. Come to think of it we even have a misunderstood and mysterious Boo Radley type character derived from actual folklore, called The Goatman lurking about. A February selection of my Southern Lit club, I found it a very engaging read !! 5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="16729440389828374258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1735440404" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1735440404" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4809022-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295019472p2/4809022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1735440404?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/4809022-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780307475268" href="/book/show/8511156-the-bottoms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4809022-stephen?shelf=favourites-fiction">favourites-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4809022-stephen?shelf=my-top-5-books-read-in-2016">my-top-5-books-read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1735440404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5883962250272709653">Been meaning to read this one for ages but had been put off by the title due to British/US language differences - "The Bottoms" conjures up an image of toilet humour to a British reader (like the "Captain Underpants" books that my kids used to love when they were in primary school) but I soon discovered that it instead refers to the "Bottoms" of the swampy river where the story takes place.<br/><br/>Absolutely loved this one once I got into it - great characters and really felt that you were in the time a</span>
  <span id="freeText5883962250272709653" style="display:none">Been meaning to read this one for ages but had been put off by the title due to British/US language differences - "The Bottoms" conjures up an image of toilet humour to a British reader (like the "Captain Underpants" books that my kids used to love when they were in primary school) but I soon discovered that it instead refers to the "Bottoms" of the swampy river where the story takes place.<br /><br />Absolutely loved this one once I got into it - great characters and really felt that you were in the time and place where it all happened. A combination of 1930s Southern racial issues and Ku Klux Klan and a serial killer thriller. To get 5 stars, you need a great ending too and this certainly had that - couldn't get through it fast enough at the end which was one of the most thrilling ever.<br /><br />As this was my first Joe Lansdale book, I am pretty excited about having discovered a new favourite author with loads of books that I've yet to read as well ! <br /><br />Highly recommended !</span>
  <a data-text-id="5883962250272709653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/786847330?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kirk Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kirk Smith" href="/user/show/15749169-kirk-smith">Kirk Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15749169-kirk-smith?shelf=southern-literature">southern-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer786847330" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7678391495681217002"> Everything I have read by Joe R. Lansdale has been good. Really good storytelling that easily draws me in. I cared about every character including the families pet hound. The Bottoms was the best of the three I have read. Told from the point of view of a twelve year old boy helping his father, the town constable, to solve the mystery behind a string of brutal murders. Everything you might ever need to know about the piney woods of East Texas.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9309403342484370622">That was a great read, however sad and disturbing it be. Joe R Lansdale knows the perfect way to tell a tale, short and sweet, but packs a punch full of emotions. His style of writing is very easy going, like he's sitting at a campfire or just shooting the shit out on a hike and you're listening to him fully as to pass the time.   <span id="freeText9309403342484370622" style="display:none">That was a great read, however sad and disturbing it be. Joe R Lansdale knows the perfect way to tell a tale, short and sweet, but packs a punch full of emotions. His style of writing is very easy going, like he's sitting at a campfire or just shooting the shit out on a hike and you're listening to him fully as to pass the time. He's got a good sense of humor, even for times where it wasn't meant to be funny... <br /><br />And his language is authentic, the scenes come to life and everything seems beautiful and disturbingly real. I've only read three of his books now, and they all have that same rustic vibe. <br /><br /> Perfect reads for anyone who enjoys history and horror, and all that deep south goodness!</span>

<div id="review_14912034" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14912034" />
    <a title="Bill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/810550-bill"><img alt="Bill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462234651p2/810550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/14912034?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill" href="/user/show/810550-bill">Bill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/810550-bill?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14912034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6141371408779213250">Joe R. Lansdale is predominantly known as a horror writer, but lookie here: The Bottoms won the Edgar Award (Mystery) for best novel. <br/>Now, despite being a mystery, there weren't any big surprises for me, but where the novel truly shines is as the coming of age story of a 13 year-old boy in the early 1930s.<br/><br/>I was surprised at what a quick read this was. For some reason I was under the impression that this was a denser read, but in no way was I disappointed at that. I'm a big fan of less is more. L</span>
  <span id="freeText6141371408779213250" style="display:none">Joe R. Lansdale is predominantly known as a horror writer, but lookie here: The Bottoms won the Edgar Award (Mystery) for best novel. <br />Now, despite being a mystery, there weren't any big surprises for me, but where the novel truly shines is as the coming of age story of a 13 year-old boy in the early 1930s.<br /><br />I was surprised at what a quick read this was. For some reason I was under the impression that this was a denser read, but in no way was I disappointed at that. I'm a big fan of less is more. Lansdale writes in a very economical fashion, but I was totally drawn in to the sense of place and time in this story. The characters were well developed, and the description and feel of racial tensions are worthy of Harper Lee's classic.<br />The only thing that could have been better was maybe being rocked or<br />blindsided by a revelation at the end, and for this reason only, my rating will fall only a smidgen short of awesome. <br />On second thought, as I write this review, images from the story are still flashing through my mind, and there are feelings that I think will continue to linger for a while yet. I love books that will do that to me. <br />So, 5 stars it is. It's such a fast read, but it'll take a long while to shake the feeling of East Texas in the 1930s. Highly recommended.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6141371408779213250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1101733081" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1101733081" />
    <a title="Glenn Rolfe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16739484-glenn-rolfe"><img alt="Glenn Rolfe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600661301p2/16739484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1101733081?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Glenn Rolfe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Glenn Rolfe" href="/user/show/16739484-glenn-rolfe">Glenn Rolfe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780892967049" href="/book/show/2033745.The_Bottoms">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1101733081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12032087838470702452">After reading a couple of Lansdale's newer books, and hearing how much other writer's loved his work, I decided to check out the novel that seems to get the most hype, THE BOTTOMS. This one had been on my radar for the last couple years. I decided to grab a copy from my local library, and I'm glad I did. <br/>While not as perfect as TO KILL A MOCKINGBIRD (Harper Lee), THE BOTTOMS is definitely in the same ballpark of great American literature. An amazing cast of characters are brought to life and tos</span>
  <span id="freeText12032087838470702452" style="display:none">After reading a couple of Lansdale's newer books, and hearing how much other writer's loved his work, I decided to check out the novel that seems to get the most hype, THE BOTTOMS. This one had been on my radar for the last couple years. I decided to grab a copy from my local library, and I'm glad I did. <br />While not as perfect as TO KILL A MOCKINGBIRD (Harper Lee), THE BOTTOMS is definitely in the same ballpark of great American literature. An amazing cast of characters are brought to life and tossed into this excellent tale of murder, mystery, and the evil that men do. <br /><br />Based down south back in the 1930's, a young boy, Harry, and his sister Tom, find a brutalized body barbwired to a tree down by the river. Their father, Jacob, the town constable, sets out to try and figure who could have done such a thing. Race plays a major role in the story adding depth and tension to an already poignant piece. More bodies turn up, and the town, led by a Klan loving bastard named Nation, is convinced the killer is black and set there eyes upon an old man living in a shack in the bottoms. <br />There are plenty of twists and turns throughout. Harry's part in all of this makes for a great coming-of-age story, as well. We see plenty of what is so wrong with America (then and now), but Lansdale also reminds us that there is goodness, even in those we think are among the lost.<br /><br />My thoughts:<br />A terrific novel, filled with intrigue and suspense, wonderful descriptive narratives, characters you won't soon forget, and that old life lesson–never judge a book by its cover.<br />I did know who the killer was fairly early on, but that did not take away from my enjoyment of the book. Don't wait as long as I did to pick this one up! <br /><br />I give THE BOTTOMS 5 stars. Definitely a book every writer should read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12032087838470702452" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2414089592" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2414089592" />
    <a title="Cody | CodysBookshelf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf"><img alt="Cody | CodysBookshelf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592500568p2/56352820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2414089592?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cody | CodysBookshelf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cody | CodysBookshelf" href="/user/show/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf">Cody | CodysBookshelf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780892967049" href="/book/show/2033745.The_Bottoms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf?shelf=joe-r-lansdale">joe-r-lansdale</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2414089592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6814398199257212829">Damn it, Joe Lansdale, you broke my heart. Again.<br/><br/><i>The Bottoms</i> is one of this author’s more critically acclaimed novels, and rightfully so. It’s an involving and impeccably told mystery set in East Texas in 1933 — so, yes, this novel is right in Lansdale’s wheelhouse. Depression-era stories are what the Mojo Storyteller does best, and this is a corker.<br/><br/>Told in the first-person perspective of an old man looking back on his youth, this is about a series of murders going on in a small southern town — </span>
  <span id="freeText6814398199257212829" style="display:none">Damn it, Joe Lansdale, you broke my heart. Again.<br /><br /><i>The Bottoms</i> is one of this author’s more critically acclaimed novels, and rightfully so. It’s an involving and impeccably told mystery set in East Texas in 1933 — so, yes, this novel is right in Lansdale’s wheelhouse. Depression-era stories are what the Mojo Storyteller does best, and this is a corker.<br /><br />Told in the first-person perspective of an old man looking back on his youth, this is about a series of murders going on in a small southern town — and the boy’s father, the Constable, tries piecing things together. Told in Lansdale’s assured, country-fried style, this is a satisfying and enthralling yarn filled with easily likable characters and a strong sense of location.<br /><br />I debated taking off points for figuring out the mystery halfway through, but I still had fun — despite my sneaking suspicions. <i>The Bottoms</i> is more about the journey than the destination, anyway. A blurb calls this an “R-rated version of <i>The Andy Griffith Show</i>,” and . . . yeah, that about hits the nail on the head. Highly recommended! </span>
  <a data-text-id="6814398199257212829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1278012731" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

The only reason I'm not giving it 5 stars is because it was a bit predictable and I had guessed early on who the killer was.<br/>Still, a great southern dark mystery, beautifully written and with some very likeable and memorable characters. <br/>This was my first novel by Lansdale, it won't be the last. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3169393266" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3169393266" />
    <a title="Kyra Leseberg (Roots &amp; Reads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5899398-kyra-leseberg-roots-reads"><img alt="Kyra Leseberg (Roots &amp; Reads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523718393p2/5899398.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3169393266?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyra Leseberg (Roots &amp; Reads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyra Leseberg (Roots &amp; Reads)" href="/user/show/5899398-kyra-leseberg-roots-reads">Kyra Leseberg (Roots &amp; Reads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3169393266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2687373325683573427">3.5 stars<br/><br/>Harry Crane is an old man now with plenty of time to reflect on the past.  What he remembers most vividly is his childhood in Marvel Creek, Texas.<br/><br/>In 1933, Harry was 11 years old.  He spent most of his time roaming the woods with his younger sister Tom (short for Thomasina) and their faithful dog Toby.  Their father is the local constable who also farms and owns the town barbershop and their mama is a kind and beautiful woman treated as an equal by her husband (a rarity in that era).<br/><br/>Thei</span>
  <span id="freeText2687373325683573427" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />Harry Crane is an old man now with plenty of time to reflect on the past.  What he remembers most vividly is his childhood in Marvel Creek, Texas.<br /><br />In 1933, Harry was 11 years old.  He spent most of his time roaming the woods with his younger sister Tom (short for Thomasina) and their faithful dog Toby.  Their father is the local constable who also farms and owns the town barbershop and their mama is a kind and beautiful woman treated as an equal by her husband (a rarity in that era).<br /><br />Their lives change dramatically on the evening Harry and Tom venture too far into the woods and discover the mutilated body of a woman.<br /><br />Harry's father, Jacob, is determined to identify the woman and locate her killer but the white population of Marvel Creek isn't too worried about the death of a black woman.  When the body of another woman is discovered, only then does the town begin to worry about a looming threat to white women.<br /><br />Jacob's investigation creates a stir in the segregated community and sets in motion a series of events that will change the small town forever.<br /><br />An old black man named Mose is questioned when circumstancial evidence is discovered.  Though Mose is released, a crowd gathers to be both judge and jury.  Harry and Jacob are unable to save Mose from a (<i>*warning: graphic*</i>) brutal lynching.<br /><br />When months pass without the discover of another body, the town is lulled into a sense of safety and belief they've taken care of the threat.<br />But the killer is still among them... and now Tom is in danger.<br /><br />I don't want to give too much away!  Harry's narration offers comfort in this dark story as he shares his innocent childhood thoughts and perspectives with the added insight he has gained over his lifetime.<br /><br /><b>The Bottoms</b> is a horror story about a serial killer on the loose in a small town but it's also a horror story about the town itself.  Racism runs rampant in Marvel Creek and the threat of the KKK and lynch mob mentality is just as dangerous as the killer preying on local women.<br /><br />There are several similarities between <b>The Bottoms</b> and <b>To Kill a Mockingbird</b>.  Jacob is very much like Atticus Finch in his fight for fairness and justice.  Harry and Tom mirror Jem and Scout in personality.  The authors both use adult narrators sharing childhood memories.  <b>TKAM</b> had the mystery of Boo Radley, <b>The Bottoms</b> has the mystery of The Goat Man. Both are set in small Southern towns and center around a violent crime with a black man unjustly accused.<br /><br />All of that said, <b>The Bottoms</b> stands on its own.  It's horrific and graphic in several instances while managing moments of beauty and nostalgia interspersed with humor, thanks to the innocence of childhood. <br /><br />I recommend <b>The Bottoms</b> to readers who enjoy historical fiction, horror, and mystery/crime.<br /><br />For more reviews, visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.rootsandreads.wordpress.com">www.rootsandreads.wordpress.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2687373325683573427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1742512789" />
    <a title="Andy Weston" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/313206-andy-weston"><img alt="Andy Weston" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1190073185p2/313206.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1742512789?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy Weston" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy Weston" href="/user/show/313206-andy-weston">Andy Weston</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1742512789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2811900315994348671">Set in East Texas in the years of the depression this is part murder mystery, part coming of age, and part historical novel and surely one of Joe Lansdale's finest, though that will be for debate, I have read several Lansdale and they all have 5 stars from me. <br/><br/>The story is narrated by 11 year old Harry Collins from his rest home bed many years later. There are issues of race and the KKK play a role throughout. Life in The Bottoms, a deprived and poor area of East Texas, is described wonderfully </span>
  <span id="freeText2811900315994348671" style="display:none">Set in East Texas in the years of the depression this is part murder mystery, part coming of age, and part historical novel and surely one of Joe Lansdale's finest, though that will be for debate, I have read several Lansdale and they all have 5 stars from me. <br /><br />The story is narrated by 11 year old Harry Collins from his rest home bed many years later. There are issues of race and the KKK play a role throughout. Life in The Bottoms, a deprived and poor area of East Texas, is described wonderfully by Lansdale, and though the subject matter is often dark his characters have humour and warmth. <br /><br />The strongest part of the novel is the last chapter, the climax, and there is a section following that lets the reader know what went in to happen to the cast - a welcomed feature that is almost read with a tear in the eye. <br /><br />It's probably Lansdale's most famous book to date, and surely not far off a classic of contemporary American literature.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2811900315994348671" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Y+YtqOTW4/zHvBK6s0JQU1QMRdFeBlBv30BwEcffZyAQuZHRQrZFo5NFnR2xPsl5OSaXdBv5zIhHR+oPKyWQGg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KuTcdbU3b+99Tu8OgGtovF6uhoXTidAJK/g9M98SY31Zu2AME1fJsCm3YKmCF/GWM4RUIJZ2TO6z/6ctM+iURw==')})
  }

Macondo, quindici anni, quoziente intellettivo da capogiro, lettore vorace con il mito di Sherlock Holmes e Martin Mystère, una passione inconfessata per la Bea, vuole scoprire che cosa c\'è davvero nel suo passato. È una zona buia troppo grande per ignorarle, ma l\'amatissima nonna, l’anticonformista artista cilena roçío Sánchez, che pur conosce ogni verità, è determinata a rivelarla solo dopo il traguardo dei diciotto anni: nel frattempo custodisce ciò che c\'è da custodire dentro una scatola inaccessibile, lassù, sull\'ultimo scaffale del suo studio. Animo da detective, e scatola fuori portata, Macondo comincia indagine personale, raccogliendo indizi e aneddoti che colpisce dalla TRIAD di amici di roçío spesso radunati a casa loro, e dai foglietti che la nonna gli scrive strappandoli da un blocchetto che porta sempre appeso al collo: un intervento alla gola le ha portato via la voce e lei rimedia così, matita alla mano. Macondo scoprirà presto di portare inscritto nel nome ben più del senso di solitudine ispirato dal paese inventato da Gabriel García Márquez: nel suo nome è racchiusa tutta la sua storia. La sua ricerca d\'identità diventa allora un cammino sia verso se stesso, sia verso chi lo ha amato, un percorso che lo conduce fino all\'istante largo, soggetto di un quadro della nonna, ma soprattutto epifania di un momento che apre le porte della consapevolezza: la famiglia non è necessariamente una struttura costruita a priori, ma può assumere le forme più diverse, spuntare in situazioni in cui i legami di sangue non ricoprono alcun ruolo, diventare uno spazio immenso per chi ama. Con una scrittura limpida e poetica, Sara fruner ci offre una riflessione insieme intensa e lieve sull\'imprevedibilità dei legami che ci forgiano. E se gli amori sono rimasti incompiuti, se sono Terminati troppo presto, ogni legame spezzato del nostro passato può avere una seconda, inattesa chance, che ci sorprende.<\/span>\n  <a       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/58971.Joe_R_Lansdale">About Joe R. Lansdale</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/58971.Joe_R_Lansdale"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1200406474p3/58971.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/58971.Joe_R_Lansdale">Joe R. Lansdale
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,507
followers
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6732091232373357950">Champion Mojo Storyteller Joe R. Lansdale is the author of over forty novels and numerous short stories. His work has appeared in national anthologies, magazines, and collections, as well as numerous foreign publications. He has written for comics, television, film, newspapers, and Internet sites. His work has been collected in more than two dozen short-story collections, and he has edited or co-e</span>
  <span id="freeText6732091232373357950" style="display:none">Champion Mojo Storyteller Joe R. Lansdale is the author of over forty novels and numerous short stories. His work has appeared in national anthologies, magazines, and collections, as well as numerous foreign publications. He has written for comics, television, film, newspapers, and Internet sites. His work has been collected in more than two dozen short-story collections, and he has edited or co-edited over a dozen anthologies. He has received the Edgar Award, eight Bram Stoker Awards, the Horror Writers Association Lifetime Achievement Award, the British Fantasy Award, the Grinzani Cavour Prize for Literature, the Herodotus Historical Fiction Award, the Inkpot Award for Contributions to Science Fiction and Fantasy, and many others. His novella <i>Bubba Ho-Tep</i> was adapted to film by Don Coscarelli, starring Bruce Campbell and Ossie Davis. His story "Incident On and Off a Mountain Road" was adapted to film for Showtime's "Masters of Horror," and he adapted his short story "Christmas with the Dead" to film hisownself. The film adaptation of his novel <i>Cold in July</i> was nominated for the Grand Jury Prize at the Sundance Film Festival, and the Sundance Channel has adapted his Hap &amp; Leonard novels for television. <br /><br />He is currently co-producing several films, among them <i>The Bottoms</i>, based on his Edgar Award-winning novel, with Bill Paxton and Brad Wyman, and <i>The Drive-In</i>, with Greg Nicotero. He is Writer In Residence at Stephen F. Austin State University, and is the founder of the martial arts system Shen Chuan: Martial Science and its affiliate, Shen Chuan Family System. He is a member of both the United States and International Martial Arts Halls of Fame. He lives in Nacogdoches, Texas with his wife, dog, and two cats.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6732091232373357950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
